# Execution Plan — Auditable Claim Ledger (2026-07-13)

Derived from docs/RAPTOR_RAG_IMPLEMENTATION_CHECKLIST.md FROZEN at commit f049041 (claim IDs = `<chunk>:L<line>` in the frozen copy).
Method: exhaustive claim extraction (14 chunks, 533 claims) → terminology reconciliation vs code (11 families) → 5W+feasibility critique per claim → deterministic parity-checked assembly.
Every claim in the implementation plan, resolved or not, appears below exactly once as an auditable action.
How to audit a row: open the frozen line, run/inspect the Required receipt, confirm the Disposition.
Companion: docs/PLAN_CRITIQUE_2026-07-13.md holds the S0–S14 sequencing rationale; this file holds the per-claim ledger.

## The Holistic End Goal — what all of this builds, end to end

*Authored by the orchestrator (not generated by the audit workflow) — this is the cohesive statement of what the executed plan produces, traced as one pipeline. Each stage names its canonical schema, its S-step, and its current state (LIVE / IN CODE / UNBUILT).*

**One sentence:** a deterministic-first library where a lay-language question reliably finds the right documents across corpora — because every document carries typed, canonical, alias-expanded metadata (concepts, facets, temporal, bibliographic) captured **once** at ingest, promoted into indexed stores, and consumed by a librarian that assigns seats deterministically — LLMs enrich and explain, but never pick final seats, and every behavior flip is gated by a frozen held-out eval.

### Stage map (ingest → answer)

**1. Ingest & chunking — structure is sacred.**
Docling parses; four deterministic routers chunk (tables/code/transcripts/prose lanes); parents preserve **mid-document `heading_path`** (the reason re-extraction was authorized — parents are the retrieval surface, and a parent that has lost its section header cannot be routed); children default to 128 tokens. `page_start` exists nowhere today and only a reingest lane can add it — that is exactly what the S3 disposition matrix decides per corpus. Canonical schema: the standardized chunk-metadata contract (P2.1/P0.5), enforced by P0.8 validators at the writer boundary. State: chunking LIVE; header-quality audit + reingest decision = S3 (in flight); chunk-schema standardization = S5/P2.1 (UNBUILT).

**2. Chunk-level extraction — RunPod burst, typed and temporal.**
After a corpus is chunk-complete (the barrier), GLiNER-ReLEX + spaCy run as a serverless RunPod flash burst: multi-account least-in-flight dispatch, saturating workers, scale-to-zero — extraction cost is bought once, at maximum speed. Wire contract `polymath.runpod_gliner_relex.v3` carries entities, relations, facts, **`temporal_captures`/`time_expressions` with char offsets** (T-HOOK-1, LIVE — 92/3,791 mark rows verified). Typed relation signatures + negation (P2.4/P2.5) kill the "Applies to uses conor" gloss rot; engine parity (P2.6) makes local Ghost B and RunPod interchangeable. State: RunPod path LIVE and gate-proven (37.2/22.6 chunks/s); parity/negation/signatures UNBUILT (S11 runs the pair burst only after they land — extraction is paid ONCE).

**3. Parent-level semantics — one pydantic contract, prompt + deterministic parse.**
Ghost A's summary call is the single seam where parent-level meaning is generated. Canonical schema: `SummaryResult` — summary + **`latent_concepts`** (≤12, `direct|inferred`, ≤3 aliases each; the "underlying/hidden concept" capture) + **`temporal_class` + `time_expressions`** (S1, in flight). The prompt asks; **deterministic Python parsers** (`parse_latent_concepts`, `parse_temporal_semantics`) clamp, validate enums, and drop malformed output with counters — the LLM proposes, code disposes. P0.8 typed-model acceptance validates at the Mongo writer. State: latent capture LIVE (contract) but coverage is only the v2 regen window — the pair has ZERO; S4 is the ONE paid pass that fills latent+aliases+temporal together (never piecemeal — standing rule).

**4. Metadata extraction — bibliographic & temporal document identity.**
T-HOOK-3 (S2): docling front-matter capture + publication-vs-file-date de-conflation → `author/title/language/document_date/source_published_at` on documents (today: ~0–1 of 681 docs have any). Deterministic backfill, no LLM. This is what makes "the book by X, from before Y" answerable and feeds card fields. State: UNBUILT, sequenced before any card rebuild.

**5. Promotion & storage — capture becomes fast search.**
The promotion layer turns artifacts into *indexed* retrieval metadata (nothing dead-ends in a side collection): parent `latent_concepts` → doc-profile concepts → `corpus_lexicon` entries keyed by `canonical_key` (`normalize_identity` — hyphenated `entity_id` convention) → the **versioned alias registry** (S5) → Qdrant payload fields (concepts, cleaned `facet_ids`, `temporal_class`) with payload indexes; `doc_summaries` holds the ONLY summary vectors (Tier-0 doc routing — parent summaries are never embedded); `librarian_cards` carry field-level provenance `{value, method, source_ids, confidence}`; Neo4j gets typed edges. Facet hygiene: the broad-alias family stamping 71–100% of every corpus loses retrieval rights by DF rule (S7, YOUR decision), so facets discriminate instead of blur. Readiness splits three ways (S6): operational / metadata-quality / temporal — `fully_enriched` stops overstating. State: lexicon/cards LIVE v0; alias registry, DF rule, readiness split, slim payload projections UNBUILT (S5–S7).

**6. Query flow — find, then hydrate.**
Query → cached vocabulary resolution (LIVE: 2.49s cold → 2ms hit, epoch-invalidated) → **alias/underlying-concept expansion** from the registry (S5) with the non-negotiables intact: the original query stays a protected lane; expansion can never drift or replace it → grounded planner (decomposer for multi-part questions; strength-first dossier, obligation-aware cap replacing the positional 6-match cap) → Tier-0 routes to documents via summary vectors → **shelf engine** assigns roles from card overlap (direct/foundational/adjacent/bridge/counterbalance) → `reservation_policy` seats corpora fairly (calibrated gate, seats-not-scores); shelf_reserve adds ≤1 bridge + ≤1 counterbalance seat (merged DARK, flips only via S8 A/B) → hierarchy descent doc → parent → child. Then the **deterministic hydration waterfall**: full text → summary → skip, budget-ruled, no LLM in assembly. State: resolution/floor/gates LIVE; expansion + planner activation + anchoring + answer-shape routing = S5/S9.

**7. Rerank & answer — one scoring authority, honest refusals.**
The fp16 cross-encoder (:8081) is the sole scoring authority (production-redesign direction — blocklists and multi-score fusion retire); timeout → rank-fusion breaker, never split-retry; support passes never rerank in parallel with embedding (Metal contention rule). Answerability is two mirrored gates: strict sufficiency drives retrieval repair, the lenient arbiter decides refusal; refusals name the nearest documents instead of stonewalling; every source keeps corpus/doc/parent-child identity and provenance. State: LIVE end-to-end; adaptive rerank budgets (P1.9) UNBUILT.

**8. The measurement spine — nothing flips without receipts.**
Frozen 58-question held-out suite + contamination firewall (LIVE, baselines: Fast 84.3% / Hybrid 90.2% / Graph 94.3% doc-hit, negatives 5/5) with preregistered thresholds (+10pts naive/cross-corpus doc-hit, no shape −5pts, negatives 5/5, latency +20%); the 16×3 regression matrix and strict-ready gates close the program (S14). Every dark feature (shelf_reserve, P2.2 multi-point) turns on only through this spine.

### Why this order and no other
Capture fields ride ONE contract change (S1) → bibliographic lands (S2) → reingest decision (S3) → ONE paid pass writes everything (S4) → deterministic rollup makes it searchable (S5) → readiness/facet hygiene make it honest (S6/S7) → cards rebuilt ONCE, shelf A/B measured (S8) → consumption features (S9/S10) → the ONE paid extraction burst with final contracts (S11) → temporal program (S12) → experiments (S13) → full gate (S14). Every "ONE" is a standing rule with a receipt trail — the two prior sequencing violations (paid summaries without the capture hook; cards built on empty feeds) cannot recur without an explicit owner waiver.

### Feasibility posture (orchestrator's own review)
Feasible with current substrate: S1–S2, S5–S8 (pure code + deterministic passes + one bounded LLM pass). Risky and gated: S4 cost rides the S3 reingest decision; S10 (multi-point) is the largest recall lever but needs its four prerequisites (all sequenced ahead of it); S12 temporal query modes are the deepest change and deliberately last of the mainline. Blocked on owner: S3 sign-off, S7 DF rule. The single biggest technical risk in the whole plan: **mixed-embedding contamination** (local mxfp8 vs RunPod fp, cosine 0.98) — the promotion gate (whole-corpus bulk only, never mixed in one collection, recall A/B first) is the guard, and it must hold through S11's burst.

### Family: librarian

### Collisions & duplicate-implementation risks (full list)

- **[latent] latent_concepts**: (a) word-collision: 'latent' also names an UNRELATED graph-discovery family — DiscoverResponse.latent_topics (backend/models/schemas.py:997, graph/orchestrator.py:5368 'signals') and trace latent_terms (schemas.py:878, polymath_mcp/tools.py:813). Never reconcile these with latent_concepts. (b) dark data: latent_concepts[].aliases are parsed+clamped but read by NOTHING (PLAN_CRITIQUE_2026-07-13.md:68,106) — S5 alias-registry must consume, not re-capture.
- **[latent] latent concept**: None beyond the latent_topics/latent_terms word-collision noted on the latent_concepts row.
- **[latent] hidden concept**: No code symbol named 'hidden*' exists anywhere in backend. Do not create one.
- **[latent] underlying concept**: Zero grep hits for 'underlying concept' in backend or the two plan docs — plan-conversation synonym only.
- **[latent] parent-level keywords**: (a) the plan's singular 'keywords' hides that it is THREE distinct Ghost A fields with different semantics (proper nouns vs transferable mechanisms vs normalized concepts); (b) keep distinct from latent_concepts — key_terms must appear verbatim in the passage, latent_concepts may be inferred.
- **[latent] tree concepts**: (a) bare field name 'concepts' means different scopes in three stores (summary_tree.concepts per node, doc_profile.concepts per doc, Qdrant doc_summary payload 'concepts') — always qualify with the collection; (b) duplicate-implementation guard: any new backfill/derivation MUST import derive_node_concepts, exactly as backfill_tree_concepts.py does.
- **[latent] tree_concepts**: Naming trap: a reader grepping for a 'tree_concepts' field finds only the script; do not add a field with this name — the Mongo field is 'concepts' on the summary_tree collection.
- **[latent] doc profile concepts**: (b) duplicate-implementation risk vs tree concepts: doc_profile.concepts IS the L4 document node's derive_node_concepts output stored a second time on documents — same lineage, one implementation, two stores. S5's rollup step 'parent latent_concepts -> doc profile concepts' (PLAN_CRITIQUE:84) must extend THIS projection, not derive a parallel doc-level concept list.
- **[latent] concept contract**: (a) CONFIRMED one-word-two-meanings: 'concept contract' names the corpus_lexicon card contract in P2.1 (checklist:813+, PLAN_CRITIQUE:36) and the Ghost A summary capture contract in P2.2/T-HOOK-2 (checklist:196-200, test_summary_semantics_latent.py:1). They live at different pipeline stages (per-parent capture vs corpus-level materialization). Any task saying just 'the concept contract' is ambiguous and must be disambiguated before implementation.
- **[latent] semantic_profile**: (a) name-adjacency hazard with THREE existing symbols: parent_chunks.semantic_chunk_type (its own aggregation source, summary_semantics.py:26 SEMANTIC_CHUNK_TYPES; card_builder.py:356,463), metadata.semantic_facets (worker.py:2916 _metadata_with_facets), and semantic_split chunking. Grep confirms zero 'semantic_profile' occurrences in backend code — it exists only at checklist:836-840.
- **[latent] central_subjects**: (b) duplicate-implementation guard: central_subjects deliberately EXCLUDES latent_concepts — those go to the separate candidate_latent_subjects field because they are LLM-generated at ingest (card_builder.py:57-63) and can corroborate but never solely qualify a direct shelf (shelf_engine.py:15-17). S5/S8 rebuild work that 'rolls latent into the card' must preserve this two-field separation, not merge latent into central_subjects. Also note the cross-store rename central_subjects->subjects in slim payloads.
- **[alias] alias**: The core concept is clean: an alias is extraction-derived identity evidence for one lexicon entry. But the bare word 'alias' is heavily overloaded elsewhere — see the 'aliases' row.
- **[alias] aliases**: FAILURE MODE (a): one word, five different concepts in five keyspaces. Only meaning 1 is normalize_identity-keyed and retrieval-live; meaning 3 is captured-but-unread; meanings 2 and 5 are separate curated stores. Any plan sentence saying just 'aliases' is ambiguous.
- **[alias] alias registry**: FAILURE MODE (b) risk: three curated alias data stores ALREADY exist (CONCEPT_ALIASES in query_semantics.py:527, entity_aliases.json neo4j_writer.py:43, canonical_families.json neo4j_writer.py:46) plus the machine-built corpus_lexicon. If S5 builds the registry as a new store instead of absorbing these, it becomes the 4th/5th parallel alias system — exactly what checklist line 817 forbids ('Keep one corpus-lexicon system; do not create a parallel concept store').
- **[alias] curated aliases**: FAILURE MODE (a)+(b): the phrase 'curated aliases' names the retrieval-side CONCEPT_ALIASES in checklist lines 63/312/465 but the graph-side canonical_families docstring (neo4j_writer.py:945) uses the identical phrase for a different mechanism in a different keyspace (canonicalize_entity_name, NFKD, alias-map). The S5 registry migration must state which of the three curated stores it absorbs.
- **[alias] vocabulary**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'vocabulary' means the query-time resolver in P1.7/P1.2 checklist items but the materialized store in the corpus_lexicon docstring and in 'concept vocabulary' (checklist:31). S5's 'corpus_lexicon/vocabulary join' only parses if vocabulary = resolver-facing projection of the same lexicon; it is not a second store.
- **[alias] corpus_lexicon**: Name drift, not concept drift: the Qdrant mirror lives in the 'schemas' collection family (corpus_{cid8}_schemas, settings.QDRANT_SCHEMAS) under kind='entity_lexicon' — three names (lexicon/schemas/entity_lexicon) for one store depending on layer.
- **[alias] lexicon entry**: P2.1 (checklist:890-901) plans SPLITTING one entry into multiple representation points (name_alias/definition/utility) each carrying canonical_key+lexicon_id — today one entry = one point with concatenated glosses. Same concept, planned finer granularity; not a duplicate store as long as lexicon_id back-pointers stay mandatory (checklist:846,896).
- **[alias] canonical_key**: FAILURE MODE (a) adjacent: 'canonical' also appears in the GRAPH keyspace — canonical_name/canonicalize_entity_name (neo4j_writer.py:848, NFKD + curated alias map) which is NOT the normalize_identity keyspace. canonical_key always means the lexicon keyspace; graph 'canonical name' is a different normalization.
- **[alias] normalize_identity**: DISTINCT from the graph normalizer normalize_entity_name (neo4j_writer.py:812: NFKD, keeps underscores because \w matches _, deletes hyphens WITHOUT inserting a space). Example divergence: 'Box2D-Lite' -> normalize_identity 'box2d lite' vs normalize_entity_name 'box2dlite'. Two legitimate keyspaces, but code that mixes them silently breaks joins (see entity_id row).
- **[alias] query expansion**: FAILURE MODE (b) watch: S5 plans 'gated query-expansion consumption' of the new alias registry. The gate machinery ALREADY exists (grounded threshold + rejected_expansions + original-lane protection + lexicon-ID rejection, checklist:597). S5 should feed registry aliases through this existing gate, not build a second expansion path.
- **[alias] strong match**: Plan-vs-code staleness: PLAN_CRITIQUE:106 says the positional 6-match cap fix 'is still open (L)', but the fix IS in code (vocabulary.py:1705 'Audit Delta 2' comment, grounded_planner.py:375). Checklist:171-172 phrases the same thing as 'obligation-aware selection'. One concept, three names, and the critique doc is behind the code.
- **[alias] entity_id**: FAILURE MODE (b) CONFIRMED IN CODE: two id builders exist. They agree on plain multi-word names but DIVERGE on hyphen/underscore/unicode names: 'Box2D-Lite' -> graph 'entity:box2dlite' vs lexicon fallback 'entity:box2d-lite'; and the lexicon fallback skips the curated entity_aliases.json merge entirely. Any lexicon entity_ids minted by the :567 fallback can fail the vocabulary.py:851 Neo4j join silently — same class of bug as the underscore-slug incident fixed in b40da18.
- **[facet] facet**: FAILURE MODE (a): one word, two runtime concepts. 'Facet' = (1) stored ingest metadata (facets/normalizer.py, polymath.facets.v1) and (2) query-side coverage lanes (_CHAT_COVERAGE_FACETS chat_orchestrator.py:239, FacetCandidate.lanes final_selector.py:51). They meet only through matching_ingest_facets/matching_vector_facets. FAILURE MODE (b): _CHAT_COVERAGE_FACETS trigger/support-term rows duplicate the same concepts as _CONTENT_FACET_ALIASES (normalizer.py:167) — on_device_llm, privacy, knowledge_graph appear verbatim in BOTH hand-maintained tables (chat_orchestrator.py:241/279/307 vs normalizer.py:296/338/168); editing one silently diverges the other.
- **[facet] facet_ids**: FAILURE MODE (a): the key 'facet_ids' changes meaning by carrier — on a chunk row it is the chunk's list; inside documents.facet_profile it is the document's list, which is then RENAMED to doc_facet_ids when copied onto Qdrant payloads (worker.py:2926 doc_facet_ids = facet_profile['facet_ids']). Any consumer that greps for 'facet_ids' without knowing the carrier gets the wrong scope. Recommend: plan text should always say chunk facet_ids vs doc_facet_ids.
- **[facet] content_facet_ids**: DISTINCT from facet_ids by design and must stay so: facet_ids is the retrievable handle (headings + gated inheritance), content_facet_ids is own-text evidence. p0_5 decontamination explicitly 'Never touches content_facet_ids' (p0_5_facet_decontamination.py:38). Sub-field 'content_facet_source' (values chunk_text/parent_summary/child_text/parent_text/document_content, normalizer.py:709) is part of the 'source' word overload — see source_level row.
- **[facet] lens**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'lens' has three meanings in this codebase: (1) SchemaLens extraction guidance (intended role, ghost_b.py:1072 docstring: 'guides extraction prompts; never creates permanent schema labels'); (2) the lens-as-facet-source misuse that P0.5 decontaminated (normalizer.py:476); (3) the chat retrieval-synthesis lens (chat_orchestrator.py:5524), a prompt-shaping construct with zero relation to facets. Plan text saying bare 'lens' in a retrieval section is ambiguous between (2) and (3). Always qualify: schema_lens vs synthesis lens.
- **[facet] facet contamination**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'contamination' also names an unrelated concept in the same checklist: held-out EVAL contamination (backend/services/eval_firewall.py:1 'contamination firewall', backend/scripts/freeze_heldout_eval.py:10, checklist P1.1 line 578/895). A grep or a checklist row saying just 'contamination' conflates data-leak-into-eval with lens-leak-into-facets. Status nuance: decontamination is merged/live (checklist:158, 68,943 parents + 271 docs) but PLAN_CRITIQUE:109 notes it deliberately LEFT the broad-alias family stamped — 'facet contamination' in the critique now mostly refers to that residue, which is a different mechanism (hand-authored aliases, not lens inheritance).
- **[facet] source_level**: FAILURE MODE (a): the 'source' word family is 5-way overloaded around facets: (1) source_level (facet provenance, this row); (2) content_facet_source (which text produced content facets: chunk_text/parent_summary/child_text/parent_text/document_content, normalizer.py:709); (3) semantic_facets.source='ingestion' (normalizer.py:723); (4) coverage-facet 'source' = ingest_facet_profile | vector_facet_probe (runtime.py:281,470); (5) source_tier / source_refs (document provenance). Checklist P0.5 'Add artifact diagnostics for facet source, confidence, and evidence' (:467, unchecked) must specify WHICH — recommend it surface source_level AND content_facet_source under those exact names.
- **[facet] DF / document frequency**: FAILURE MODE (b) risk: three DF-shaped stats could get built in parallel — (1) p0_5 parent_df (facet-level, computed ad hoc), (2) Qdrant server-side IDF (term-level, already live for BM25), (3) planned P2.1 DF/specificity fields and S7 threshold rule. S7 and P2.1 should both consume ONE persisted facet-DF stat derived from the p0_5 audit code path (audit_corpus:177-236 is the nearest existing seam; batch its cleanup backfill with S5 reindex per PLAN_CRITIQUE:86). Note checklist:156 'measure facet DF per corpus' is DONE (audit exists); the ADMISSION RULE is not.
- **[facet] broad-alias family**: FAILURE MODE (b): broad-alias suppression is already implemented TWICE — ingest-side _specific_content_alias (normalizer.py:632) and query-side SINGLE_TOKEN_ALIAS_DETECTION_KEYS (query_semantics.py:490); S7's DF rule would be a third mechanism. They gate different stages (stamping vs query alias detection vs retrieval rights) but the plan should say so explicitly or one will be rebuilt as the other. Also note _specific_content_alias only blocks ONE-WORD aliases — multiword broad aliases (e.g. 'self determination') still stamp, and the 89k/38k historical stamps remain in stores.
- **[facet] emotional_patterns**: Plan and code use the identical id. Member of the broad-alias family (S7 decision pending). Every alias in its list is one word, so under the current _specific_content_alias gate the facet can effectively no longer be stamped by alias match at all — the id survives only in legacy stored data.
- **[facet] agency_preservation**: Identical id in plan and code. Multiword aliases ('self determination', 'value alignment', 'personal meaning') still pass the one-word specificity gate, so unlike emotional_patterns this facet CAN still be stamped on new ingests — S7 cannot be treated as legacy-only cleanup for this id.
- **[librarian] librarian card**: The word 'card' names THREE different planned artifacts: (1) librarian_card.v0 per-document (built, 673 live), (2) P1.4 'corpus/shelf profile card' per-corpus (PLAN-ONLY), (3) P3.2 'bridge cards' per cross-corpus concept (PLAN-ONLY). Only (1) exists in code.
- **[librarian] librarian_card.v0**: None — plan string and code string are byte-identical.
- **[librarian] shelf**: FAILURE MODE (a) — one word, two meanings. P1.4 'Route Shelves Before Books' (checklist:622-629) and the P0.3 acceptance line "corpus_floor.skipped reports why a selected SHELF was omitted" (checklist:430) use shelf = CORPUS. P1.5/shelf_engine uses shelf = query-relative ROLE bucket. Only the role meaning exists in code; the corpus meaning is plan-only.
- **[librarian] shelf_reserve**: Near-name collision with 'shelf routing' (P1.4) — unrelated concepts. Also: docs/PLAN_CRITIQUE_2026-07-13.md:71 states 'shelf_reserve as a symbol does not exist in backend code' — STALE since merge f049041 (wave3/reserve); the symbol family now exists, dark behind SHELF_RESERVE_ENABLED=False.
- **[librarian] shelf routing**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'shelf' here means corpus, not role. Do NOT reuse librarian_card.v0 or shelf_engine names for it. Nearest existing seams: (1) slim_card_payload (card_builder.py:598) is the per-DOC routing projection the per-CORPUS card should aggregate from; (2) Tier-0 doc_summaries routing (owner architecture) is the routing stage it plugs into; (3) 'preserve user-selected corpora even when shelf routing is weak' (checklist:629) is ALREADY implemented as the corpus floor (ranking_policy.py:1682, final_selector.reserve_corpora:312).
- **[librarian] shelf roles**: None within the role meaning; see 'shelf' row for the shelf-as-corpus collision.
- **[librarian] bridge**: FAILURE MODE (b) — duplicate-implementation risk: P3.2 'bridge cards' (checklist:1141-1147, PLAN-ONLY) and 'transfer_edge' rows (checklist:319,1149-1155, PLAN-ONLY) both materialize the SAME evidence join _role_bridge computes at query time (shared principle/mechanism + different central subjects + two-sided evidence). If built without reusing shelf_engine.principle_bridge/_role_bridge criteria, the bridge notion will exist twice with drifting thresholds. Also FAILURE MODE (a): 'bridge' additionally names the answerability-gate 'LLM bridges' behavior in relationship queries (services/answerability_tuning.py family) — unrelated mechanism, same word.
- **[librarian] counterbalance**: Three artifacts share the stem with distinct jobs: role (per-query), policy keys (versioned data), card field (persisted, currently always empty — effectively PLAN-ONLY until Phase 4 LLM enrichment). Keep the card field distinct from the policy vocabulary or Phase 4 will double-implement the qualifier source.
- **[librarian] foundational**: None. Live probe honestly skipped it on the PoC pair (no qualifying candidate) — checklist P1.5 note.
- **[librarian] adjacent**: None.
- **[librarian] reading path**: Plan (checklist:668-671) wants a user-facing reading path 'not merely a flat chunk list' for librarian-mode questions; code has only the diagnostics SEED, dark behind SHELF_RESERVE_ENABLED. The answer-shaping half is to-be-built — nearest seam is the trace-metadata consumer in the frontend live-trace tabs.
- **[librarian] seat**: Consistent meaning across P0.3/P1.5 code and plan. Note there is no symbol literally named 'seat' — it lives in docstrings, diagnostics keys (seated), and reasons; grep for 'seat' not 'Seat class'.
- **[librarian] reservation**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'reserve/reservation' spans four mechanisms — lane reservation (reserve_lanes), corpus floor (3 implementations), planned-finalist reservation, and the shelf-role seat pass. Only three of the four corpus-seat paths use the shared reservation_policy gate; final_selector.reserve_corpora still applies its own _strong_score_floor (0.80 ratio && 0.35 abs) — a stricter, uncalibrated sibling.
- **[librarian] corpus floor**: FAILURE MODE (b) CONFIRMED: the corpus-floor idea is implemented three times; ranking_policy + planned_fusion share the calibrated P0.3 gate, but final_selector.reserve_corpora keeps its own discipline. The checklist itself flags it (2026-07-13 ledger, checklist:1291-1293: 'reserve_corpora still uses its own discipline; superseded by shelf_reserve in P1.5') — but that supersession claim is WRONG in code: reserve_shelf_roles seats only bridge/counterbalance roles and does not do per-corpus coverage, and reserve_corpora still executes unconditionally (final_selector.py:572) even with SHELF_RESERVE_ENABLED on. Plus FAILURE MODE (a): two diagnostics keys both named 'corpus_floor' report different mechanisms.
- **[librarian] reservation_policy**: Module name is singular-purpose but the plan sometimes says 'reservation policy' to mean the whole seat behavior including reserve_corpora — which is NOT on this module. Cite the module path when you mean the gate.
- **[temporal] temporal_class**: One name planned on FOUR carriers (document metadata spec:211, summary nodes spec:101, fact assertions spec:265, Qdrant payload spec:591). Must stay ONE enum (evergreen|slowly_evolving|versioned|event|ephemeral|unknown) fed by ONE classifier, or per-carrier drift becomes failure mode (a).
- **[temporal] time_expressions**: FAILURE MODE (a): the same name time_expressions is ALSO planned as a NEW Ghost A summary-contract field (T-HOOK-2, CHECKLIST:195-198) — summary-level time expressions, a different seam from the built chunk-level extraction capture. When S1 builds it, either persist the summary field under a distinct name or document scope explicitly: chunk-level = temporal_captures (built), summary-level = T-HOOK-2 (unbuilt).
- **[temporal] published_at**: FAILURE MODE (b): publication time is planned under TWO names in the same checklist — P2.1 gains say 'published_at / temporal_scope' (CHECKLIST:166) while T-HOOK-3 and the spec say 'source_published_at' (CHECKLIST:202, spec:207,336). CHECKLIST:200 declares T-HOOK-3 merged with P2.1 as 'one implementation', so the duplicate-build risk is acknowledged, but the field NAME is not reconciled. Pick source_published_at (spec §5.1) and treat published_at as a read-side alias only.
- **[temporal] document_date**: FAILURE MODE (a) — the family's worst instance: ONE field carries THREE meanings (publication date, file-creation date, revision date) because docling_adapter.py:210-263 funnels all of them into document_date. This is exactly what T-HOOK-3 de-conflates. Spec:230 rules document_date remains a compatibility projection during migration, then deprecated — do NOT extend new features onto it.
- **[temporal] source_published_at**: See published_at row: same concept named twice across P2.1 and T-HOOK-3; one implementation is mandated (CHECKLIST:200), name must be settled as source_published_at.
- **[temporal] episodes**: No code collision — 'episode' is unused in backend/. Design lineage is Graphiti's episode concept (spec:147-153).
- **[temporal] assertions**: Two collisions. (a1) fact_type='timestamp' EXISTS in Ghost B FACT_TYPES (backend/services/ghost_b.py:134-137) and is the tempting-but-forbidden carrier — spec:347 explicitly rules 'Do not overload fact_type=timestamp'; assertion validity is a separate envelope. (a2) superseded_at ALREADY exists with a different meaning: job-lease supersession (backend/services/ingestion/job_leases.py:435, job_control.py:60,113) and chunk superseded_by (contracts.py:115) — three lifecycles will share one word once fact_assertions.superseded_at lands; keep them namespaced by collection. Also note 'assertion' pervasively means test-assertion in scripts (e.g. backend/scripts/p0_1_summary_integrity.py:28) — grep noise, not a real conflict.
- **[temporal] temporal eligibility**: FAILURE MODE (a): do NOT confuse with the BUILT temporal_support/has_temporal machinery in the insight orchestrator (_has_temporal_source_support backend/services/graph/orchestrator.py:3003-3014, flags at :605,:1265,:5726) — that answers 'does this evidence row carry ANY date metadata' for packet curation/prompt hints; it is not validity filtering and must not be reused as the eligibility predicate. Second nearby-but-distinct seam: query_plan.py ConstraintKind 'temporal' (backend/services/retriever/query_plan.py:39, temporal_day_0 at :362-370) is lexical query-constraint tagging, not eligibility.
- **[temporal] date de-conflation**: FAILURE MODE (b) — pre-empted but watch it: T-HOOK-3 and the P2.1 'deterministic bibliographic capture/backfill' describe the same work; CHECKLIST:200 and critique S2 both pin them to ONE implementation. Residual risk is only the field-name split (published_at vs source_published_at, see those rows).
- **[temporal] temporal_unavailable**: Lands on the SAME seam as the S6 readiness split (operational vs metadata-quality vs temporal capability); the enum must live beside — not inside — fully_enriched, because fully_enriched is a pipeline-stage label (backend/services/ingestion/readiness.py:112 FULLY_ENRICHED_STAGES) that must stop implying librarian-grade or temporal-grade metadata (CHECKLIST:169-171).
- **[hierarchy] heading_path**: Failure mode (a): the typed-contract layer (contracts.ChunkMetadata) calls the identical concept section_path while every store and dataclass calls it heading_path; the P0.8 typed-writer-boundary work (open) will collide these two names at the writer seam if not reconciled.
- **[hierarchy] parent chunk**: Failure mode (a): 'parent' means three things — (1) parent_chunk; (2) TreeNode.parent_ids (summary_tree.py:95) which are MEMBER parent-chunk ids, NOT tree-parents (tree children live in child_node_ids); (3) qdrant passthrough_parent_ids (parent-chunk ids again). A reader assuming parent_ids = tree ancestry will invert the hierarchy.
- **[hierarchy] child chunk**: Failure mode (a): 'child' spans three id spaces — child_chunk ids (chunk_id), summary provenance source_child_ids (P0.1 'verify summary has child IDs' means THESE), and tree child_node_ids (P0.2 'one-child section' means THESE, they are rollup node ids). The Mongo collection for child chunks is named plain 'chunks', hiding the parent/child asymmetry (parent_chunks vs chunks).
- **[hierarchy] passthrough**: Failure mode (a): 'passthrough' elsewhere in the codebase means OpenAI-compatible provider passthrough (chat_orchestrator.py:6642, provider_presets.py:18, ghost_b.py:3974) and schema_lens id passthrough (ghost_b_local.py:322) — grep for 'passthrough' returns two unrelated subsystems.
- **[hierarchy] singleton**: Failure mode (a), strong: 'Singleton' appears ~20x in backend meaning service-instance singletons (auth.py:294, llm.py:1237, tool_registry.py:215, facet_tagger.py:42...). The P0.2 open decision 'future singleton sections physically omitted or retained as aliases' (checklist:388-390) is PLAN-ONLY — no omit/alias branch exists in summary_tree.py; today every one-child section is retained and stamped with passthrough fields.
- **[hierarchy] page_start**: Failure mode (b) variant — implemented-but-dead: the field, writers, and readers all exist, but live data is 0 populated on all four corpora (PLAN_CRITIQUE section 2 table; checklist Audit Delta 2 'parent page_start/entity char offsets are 0'). Plan S3 codifies it: 'page_start is absent everywhere and only a reingest lane can ever add it'. Any new plan item that 'adds page anchors' would duplicate this existing plumbing instead of feeding it.
- **[hierarchy] hierarchy descent**: Partial: descent over Tier-0-routed documents is BUILT; the Phase-2 item 'Descend reserved documents through tree -> parent -> child evidence' (checklist:300) — descent driven from shelf_reserve seats — is not, because shelf_reserve itself has no code symbol (PLAN_CRITIQUE section 2). Wiring risk: implementing seat-descent as a new path instead of feeding reserved doc_ids into the existing SummaryTreeNavigator would be failure mode (b).
- **[hierarchy] RAPTOR tree**: Failure mode (b), explicit: the built tree is NOT RAPTOR — RAPTOR_RAG_CRITIQUE_AND_ROADMAP.md:39 calls it 'closer to a doc-summary index + auto-merging than to RAPTOR' (no clustering, doc-gated). Meanwhile P3.1 plans a real clustering-based 'thematic RAPTOR layer' (checklist:1094,1124) as future work. Two different concepts share the name RAPTOR: the existing heading-grouped summary_tree (misnomer) and the to-be-built thematic layer. A grep-driven implementer could 'extend RAPTOR' in either place.
- **[hierarchy] summary tree**: None internally — this is the one well-named concept; but note its Qdrant home is the generically-named 'schemas' collection kind shared with the entity lexicon (LEXICON_SCHEMA_KIND, qdrant_writer.py:1184), distinguished only by payload kind field.
- **[hierarchy] doc summary**: Failure mode (a): 'summary' spans two levels — parent summaries (chunk_type='summary', Funnel A breadth, Ghost A parent_summary.v1) vs document summaries (chunk_type='doc_summary', Tier-0 routing only, '§10.2: routing card, NEVER evidence'). The owner-architecture line 'doc_summaries = only summary vectors' reads ambiguously against the live schema where parent-summary vectors dominate the naive collection. Plan phrase 'document summary tree' (checklist:1239) means the whole per-doc summary_tree, a third referent.
- **[hierarchy] boundaries**: Failure mode (a), worst in family: one word, at least four implementations plus one PLAN-ONLY (evidence_spans exact boundaries, P2.1). P0.1's open verify item and P0.2's open fixture item both say 'boundaries' but target different stores (summary provenance vs tree node extents); implementing one validator for both would be wrong, implementing two under the same name invites failure mode (b).
- **[hierarchy] mid-document header**: If this term denotes headers appearing mid-flow that should split/route chunks, that behavior already exists across THREE seams (synthetic injection pre-parse, docling section_heading blocks, page-heading demotion in the tree). A new 'mid-document header' feature built fresh would be failure mode (b); it should be specified as a change to one of these seams. The open plan work nearest to it is P0.5 'Audit OCR-corrupt heading paths and define a source-safe repair rule' (checklist:462) and plan S3's heading/OCR quality audit.
- **[extraction] ghost_b**: (a) one word, two scopes: 'ghost_b' names BOTH the whole extraction stage (any engine writes ghost_b_extractions — including runpod_flash) AND specifically services/ghost_b.py's provider-LLM lane. The engine enum makes this concrete: engine='local' now means a private provider LLM running ghost_b.py's contract, while the old GLiNER/GLiREL sidecar is 'legacy_local' (extraction_contract.py:15-19) — the word 'local' silently changed meaning across the rename.
- **[extraction] GLiNER**: (a) 'GLiNER' means two different models in two places: local lane = entity-only GLiNER + separate GLiREL for relations; RunPod lane = gliner-relex joint model doing both. P2.7b's 'GLiNER-ReLEX + spaCy windows... in the worker' is the remote stack; the local stack is a DIFFERENT composition producing the same artifact shape — this is exactly the parity surface P2.6/P2.7 must measure, not an accidental duplicate.
- **[extraction] GLiREL**: (b) duplicate-implementation risk (intentional, must stay measured): relation extraction exists twice — GLiREL locally vs gliner-relex remotely (and a third time via provider-LLM RelationItems in ghost_b.py). GLiREL is NOT shipped in the RunPod worker (app.py deps list gliner+spacy only, app.py:538-539), so 'burst runs the full local stack remotely' (P2.7b) is currently false in the strict sense — the burst runs the RELEX stack, not the GLiNER+GLiREL stack.
- **[extraction] spaCy**: None serious, but note the asymmetry: spaCy exists ONLY in the RunPod worker; the local GLiREL lane does its own sentence windowing without spaCy (glirel_infer.py). 'spaCy windows' in P2.7b describes the remote stack only.
- **[extraction] relations**: (a) one word, four layers (wire relation / durable artifact / graph edge / lexicon projection) — all the same concept flowing downstream, but line-item plan language like 'relation artifact' (P2.4) means the ghost_b_extractions row, not the Neo4j edge. Separately, P2.1 PLANS 'associated_concepts' (co-occurrence associations) and explicitly orders them kept DISTINCT from typed factual relations — associated_concepts has zero code today; do not implement it as another relations[] field.
- **[extraction] typed signatures**: (b) HIGH duplicate-implementation risk: P2.5 reads as green-field ('build a reviewed compatibility table', 'annotate signature_valid') but the table and enforcement ALREADY exist under the domain_range name — and current behavior is STRONGER than the plan wants (it remaps/warns; P2.5 says annotate-only, no drop/remap). Implementing signature_valid beside _apply_domain_range would double the mechanism. Correct move: evolve DOMAIN_RANGE_MAP into the reviewed table and demote remap to annotation, one mechanism.
- **[extraction] negation**: (a) 'negation' already means something else in shipped code: retriever-side negated-query-concept filtering (query_plan.py/vocabulary.py). P2.4's negation is extraction-side and has NO code counterpart. Nearest seams: RelationItem (ghost_b.py:1988) for the negated field, _EVIDENCE_STOPWORDS/_evidence_token_overlap (ghost_b.py:682,690) for token preservation, and the worker's spaCy parse (app.py:292) for evidence-sentence boundaries.
- **[extraction] utility gloss**: (a) THREE-way word collision: 1) 'utility' is also a query-MODEL KIND (settings.py:739, chat_orchestrator.py:6974 resolve_query_model_kind(user_id,'utility')) — a cheap-LLM role, nothing to do with glosses; 2) 'gloss' is also UNIVERSAL_ENTITY_GLOSSES (ghost_b.py:217-223) — prompt-only entity-type disambiguation glosses, explicitly 'not consumed by any storage code'; 3) siblings retrieval_gloss/embedding_gloss are different fields — the checklist's 'one compromise gloss vector' critique (line ~892) refers to embedding_gloss being the single embedded surface, and the planned representation_method='utility' point (line 911) would embed utility_gloss content as its own vector. representation_method itself is PLAN-ONLY (only test fixture mentions of utility_gloss exist outside these files).
- **[extraction] engine parity**: (a) 'parity' means three unrelated things in this repo: 1) P2.6/P2.7 engine/extraction parity (this row — measurement harness is PLAN-ONLY, no comparison script exists); 2) Mongo<->Qdrant eligible-ID parity in lexicon backfill (backend/scripts/backfill_corpus_lexicon.py:516, corpus_lexicon.py:2734); 3) runpod-EMBED cosine parity promotion gate (P1.9, checklist line ~790: local-mxfp8 vs remote-fp = 0.98). When the plan says 'parity compare' in P2.7 it means engine-vs-engine yield/quality on the SAME chunks — nothing shipped does that today.
- **[extraction] RunPod**: (a) 'RunPod' names two lanes with different contracts and different workers: extraction (runpod_flash_extractor/, polymath.runpod_gliner_relex.vN) and embedding (runpod_flash_embedder/, polymath.runpod_embed.v1, embedder.py mode='runpod'). NOT a duplicate implementation — the embed lane deliberately imports _AccountDispatcher and _submit_and_wait from runpod_flash_extraction.py (embedder.py:581), so routing/polling exists once. Keep it that way: any P2.7b dispatch changes land in runpod_flash_extraction.py and both lanes inherit.
- **[extraction] burst orchestration**: (a) 'burst' is used for three unrelated things: extraction bursts (this row), embed bursts (embedder.py:8,62), and upload-admission bursts ('500-file simultaneous burst', ingestion/admission.py:12) plus incidental 'burst-load DNS blip' in llm.py. (b) build-vs-built split inside P2.7b itself: account routing/failover is DONE; disposition matrix, chunk-complete barrier, eligible-chunk manifest, per-burst chunks/sec + worker-seconds + cost-per-1k-chunks recording have NO code — grep 'barrier|manifest|disposition' in backend/services/ingestion returns nothing relevant. Nearest seam for the barrier: worker.py pass_plan/batch machinery (batches.py INGEST_PROFILES) which already sequences queryable-vs-enrichment passes.
- **[extraction] disposition matrix**: No code symbol, no Mongo field. It is a GATE artifact, not a config: S3 (PLAN_CRITIQUE:82) produces it from the heading/OCR audit and it must precede S4's paid pass and S11's burst. Nearest existing seams: (1) per-corpus engine stamp resolved by resolve_extraction_contract (extraction_contract.py:164 — corpus-level extraction config already exists and is the natural home for a disposition field), (2) corpus strict-readiness (services/ingestion/readiness.py) which P2.7 already plans to wire extraction/concept readiness into. Risk (b): teams could encode disposition twice — once as a doc/table for sign-off and again ad hoc as engine toggles; make the corpus settings field the single source and render the sign-off table from it.
- **[extraction] wire contract**: (a) 'contract' is overloaded FOUR ways in this family: 1) this wire contract (runpod_gliner_relex.vN, request/response shape); 2) the embed wire contract polymath.runpod_embed.v1 (embedder.py:63-67, different worker); 3) the durable ARTIFACT schema polymath.extract.v1/v2 (ghost_b_extractions.schema_version — survives in Mongo, wire does not); 4) ExtractionContract (extraction_contract.py:82 — which-engine-runs resolution, no wire at all). Also note the deliberate name drift time_expressions (wire) vs temporal_captures (artifact): SAME concept, two names on either side of _validate_wire_result — cite both when auditing T-HOOK-2 backfills.
- **[extraction] provenance**: (a) one word, four shipped mechanisms plus one planned taxonomy: plan sentences using bare 'provenance' must be resolved per-context — P0.1/P0.8 mean extractor/summary_model stamps, P2.8 means lexicon source-ID lists, P2.1/P2.2 mean the FOUR-CLASS taxonomy (extracted/derived/attested/generated) which is PLAN-ONLY (grep provenance_class = zero hits; nearest seam = corpus_lexicon entry builder + _lexicon_payload). Risk (b): the four-class field could get implemented separately on lexicon entries, Qdrant representation points, and cards; it should be one enum defined once (corpus_lexicon) and projected.
- **[readiness] fully_enriched**: Failure mode (a): one string, three scopes — document ingest_stage value, corpus readiness status value, and a batch-state boolean. Grep hits are not interchangeable. Plan S6 explicitly wants fully_enriched to STOP implying librarian-grade metadata; today it already means only operational completeness (artifacts+projections+verification), never bibliographic quality.
- **[readiness] strict ready (Definition Of Strict Ready)**: Failure mode (b) HIGH RISK: no strict_ready symbol exists anywhere in backend (grep -rniE 'strict[_ -]read' backend/ = zero hits), yet ~80% of its definition is ALREADY computed by compute_corpus_readiness (queryable/summary/tree-sync/lexicon-projection/no-failed-jobs/denominator exclusions, readiness.py:1105+). Building strict_ready as a parallel computation would duplicate corpus_readiness.v2. It should be an extension of that snapshot (add: ontology-violation count, extraction/concept promotion gate — 'unpromoted_extraction_docs' already counted at readiness.py:456-457,1008 — and 3-tier smoke-probe receipts). Failure mode (a) inside the plan itself: 'strict_ready' is ALSO the top value of the temporal capability enum (temporal_unavailable|partial|strict_ready, checklist:210) — same word, corpus publication gate vs temporal capability tier.
- **[readiness] readiness (unqualified)**: Failure mode (a) CONFIRMED, 5-way: 'readiness' names five distinct mechanisms. Worst sub-collision: retrieval_readiness.py's class is literally named CorpusReadinessReport (:29) while ingestion/readiness.py owns the 'corpus_readiness' Mongo collection — same noun, disjoint semantics (schema-exists vs enrichment-complete). Any new plan work saying 'readiness' must pick a qualifier.
- **[readiness] operational readiness**: Failure mode (b): 'operational readiness' has NO code symbol of its own — it is a plan-side rename of the existing corpus_readiness.v2 computation. S6's readiness split should be implemented as a field split INSIDE corpus_readiness (e.g. readiness.operational / readiness.metadata_quality / readiness.temporal), not as a new service; otherwise the same gates get computed twice (readiness.py already reconciles projections via lexicon_ready, summary_tree_index_ready, document_profile_index_ready mins at :376,:441,:454).
- **[readiness] metadata-quality (readiness)**: No code symbol, no store field, no grep hit for metadata_quality anywhere in backend/. To-be-built. Nearest seams: (1) librarian_cards presence per doc (card_builder.py), (2) the S2/T-HOOK-3 bibliographic backfill fields once they land on documents, (3) facet-precision leftovers from P0.5 decontamination. Must be a NEW leg of corpus_readiness, gated separately from fully_enriched per S6.
- **[readiness] temporal capability**: Two collisions. (a) 'temporal_support' already exists in models/schemas.py meaning 'this graph packet's evidence has dates' — do not reuse that name for the capability tier. (a-bis) the enum's top value 'strict_ready' collides with the corpus-level Definition Of Strict Ready (see strict ready row): one word, two gates at two scopes. Recommend the enum live as corpus_readiness.temporal_capability with values temporal_unavailable|temporal_partial|temporal_strict to break the collision.
- **[readiness] publication gate**: Failure mode (a): the verb 'publish' already has a DIFFERENT code meaning in this family — corpus_lexicon.finalize_corpus_lexicon_index docstring 'reconcile ... then publish readiness' (corpus_lexicon.py:2966) means flipping lexicon_state to lexicon_ready, not card publication. A 'publication gate' grep will hit the lexicon path first. To-be-built: a check in build_librarian_cards/card consumption that requires corpus_readiness.status (or future strict_ready/metadata_quality legs) before cards become retrieval-visible.
- **[readiness] reconciliation**: Failure mode (a): one plan word, at least six distinct code mechanisms that share only the invariant 'durable stores must agree; job/failure rows are not truth'. One member is PLAN-ONLY: 'scheduled ownership reconciliation with report-only default' (checklist:515, unchecked) — nearest seam scripts/orphan_ownership_manifest.py (P0.6 dry-run manifest) + services/ingestion/repair_scheduler.py. Failure mode (b) watch: S6 defines operational readiness AS 'projections reconcile' — the reconcile results are ALREADY folded into readiness via lexicon_ready/summary_tree_index_ready/document_profile_index_ready mins; a new operational-readiness implementation must consume these, not re-derive them.
- **[retrieval] tier**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'tier' names four unrelated things — RetrievalTier store strategy; SourceChunk.source_tier retriever-provenance label; Tier-0 document-routing layer (not a RetrievalTier value); tier_chunker's ingestion format Tiers A/B/C. Any plan sentence saying just 'tier' must disambiguate.
- **[retrieval] qdrant_only**: None beyond the checklist sometimes writing 'Fast' — eval_metrics.py:214 is the authoritative alias map.
- **[retrieval] qdrant_mongo**: Watch qdrant_mongo vs qdrant_mongo_graph: several call sites collapse graph→qdrant_mongo silently on Neo4j-disabled (chat_orchestrator.py:3952-3953, graph/orchestrator.py:8633-8637); diagnostics carry requested_tier vs effective_tier (models/_schemas_legacy.py:1204-1205) to keep this honest.
- **[retrieval] grounded planner**: FAILURE MODE (a): bare 'planner' is ambiguous — the deterministic query planner (retriever/query_plan.py, QueryPlanV2) is a different component from the LLM grounded_planner; query_plan.py:838 itself notes reference resolution 'belongs to the grounded planner, not topic rules'. The critique's 'positional 6-match planner cap' (S5) is in the deterministic/vocabulary path, not grounded_planner.py. Always qualify: query planner (deterministic) vs grounded planner (LLM).
- **[retrieval] anchoring**: FAILURE MODE (a), severe: 'anchor' means four things — (1) P1.3 conversation/open-book anchors (NO code: zero hits for session/conversation/accepted anchors; all 8 P1.3 boxes open, checklist:615-627); (2) DocumentAnchorRetriever title-recall lane (exists, live); (3) graph anchor entities; (4) summary key_point child anchors. P2.8's 'document-anchor protection' (checklist:1110) refers to sense (2) + lane protection, not P1.3. Nearest existing seam for P1.3: DocumentAnchorRetriever + ranking_policy anchor-confidence priors (76-96) + conversation service (services/conversation.py) — anchors-as-priors machinery already exists per-query and needs a session-carryover feed, not a new ranker.
- **[retrieval] answer shape**: FAILURE MODE (b), mild: the same value is stored under answer_shape (plan) and answer_type (probe) — unify on answer_shape when touching the probe contract. P1.6 'Route By Answer Shape' is only partially built: classifier + threshold calibration + breadth/enumeration heuristics exist; formal shape policies, summary scaffolds, hydrate-before-cite, sibling expansion, dynamic-K-by-score-cliff are all open (checklist:688-699, 0/5 checked). New P1.6 work must extend answer_shape consumers, not add a second shape classifier.
- **[retrieval] answerability**: One concept, two INTENTIONAL mirror implementations — chat refusal gate vs retriever repair sufficiency (documented at ranking_policy.py:1080-1087: 'Do not loosen criticality here'). Not a duplicate to merge; it IS a duplicate-implementation risk if someone tunes one side only — all shared knobs must go through answerability_tuning.py. Secondary risk (b): three sufficiency-producer branches in retriever/__init__.py:3159-3200 each rebuild the same payload shape by hand; the 'source' field is the only discriminator.
- **[retrieval] lane coverage**: BOTH failure modes. (a) One word, two meanings: retriever 'lane' = QueryPlan recall lane (lane_id, role core/original); chat 'lane' = EvidencePlan side (a comparison side needing min_sources distinct docs). The plan says 'lane coverage' for both. (b) Duplicate implementation: evidence_allocation.lane_coverage (unit-tested) vs chat_orchestrator._evidence_lane_coverage (production) compute the same strong-score/distinct-doc coverage; production never calls the tested one, so tests certify dead code while the live copy drifts (chat's adds doc_names/chunk_ids/best_score). Chat DOES delegate select_lane_support/cap_chunks_per_doc to evidence_allocation (chat_orchestrator.py:64-68, 4422) — coverage should be delegated the same way.
- **[retrieval] reranker**: No name collision. Plan splits its future into two checklist ids that share a number (both 'P1.9' — critique C4 flags the duplicate section id): Qdrant hot-path audit vs adaptive rerank. Production redesign makes CE the SOLE scoring authority (checklist:129 context) — any new 'scorer' term should resolve to this component.
- **[retrieval] evidence atom**: FAILURE MODE (b), mild: 'concept:*' atoms are minted by two independent generators — query_semantics.concept_groups (concept:{group.key}) and retriever lane-id synthesis (concept:{lane_id}, retriever/__init__.py:3144). The strings look identical downstream but the namespaces differ (curated concept keys vs lane slugs); a lane id that happens to equal a concept key would silently alias. Chat gate consumes both without distinguishing (chat_orchestrator.py:962-990).
- **[retrieval] protected lane**: FAILURE MODE (a): three distinct 'protection' mechanisms share the verb — (1) protected recall lanes (this row); (2) corpus reservation seats (reservation_policy.py:1-27: 'protection is what shields a candidate from the overflow trim', calibrated bound, P0.3); (3) per-doc-cap protect_fn shielding per-side support chunks (evidence_allocation.py:225). P2.8's 'document-anchor protection' (checklist:1110-1111) would be a FOURTH protect mechanism — wire it through reservation_policy's single-discipline contract, not a new ad-hoc shield. P1.2's 'exact-string lane' has no dedicated symbol (PLAN-ONLY half); nearest seam is the exact-query candidate protection at retriever/__init__.py:2522.
- **[retrieval] fusion**: FAILURE MODE (a), severe: four mechanisms answer to 'fusion'. Sense 4 (multi-score fusion) is scheduled for retirement while sense 1 (planned fusion) is load-bearing and recently consolidated with ranking_policy (checklist:414, 1293) — a plan sentence like 'retire fusion' or 'candidate counts before/after fusion' (checklist:1246) is executable only after naming which sense. No duplicate implementation risk: the four do different jobs at different stages.
- **[retrieval] hydration**: Code hydration = chunk-text enrichment, and it EXISTS. Two plan usages are to-be-built policies on this same seam: P1.6 'hydrate child/parent evidence before treating a generated summary as a citation' (checklist:693-694, open) and the owner-architecture deterministic waterfall (full→summary→skip) which supersedes the child_summary HYDRATION_MODE default. Minor (a): ingestion _rehydrate_* is an unrelated deserialization idiom — don't count those call sites when auditing hydration. Build P1.6/waterfall inside hydrate.py's mode dispatch, not as a parallel module (duplicate-implementation risk if a 'summary scaffold hydrator' appears elsewhere).
- **[retrieval] Tier-0**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'Tier-0' is NOT a RetrievalTier — it precedes all three tiers as document routing; checklist:208 'Tier-0/Fast/Hybrid/Graph' correctly treats it as a fourth stage, but bare 'tier' sentences conflate them. Checklist Phase 2 'Tier-0 candidate gen wiring' (critique table row) = flipping/finishing the TIER0_ROUTING-gated path that already exists at retriever/__init__.py:1707 — do NOT build a second router. Note tier0.py's own docstring ('zero query-path call sites', line 8) is stale: the gated call site exists. Adjacent-but-distinct store: Mongo librarian_cards (card_builder.py) — cards degrade TO the Tier-0 document path (card_builder.py:262, checklist:285), they are not the same artifact.
- **[eval] held-out**: Identifier drift, not concept drift: plan and critique say 56 questions ('the held-out 56', PLAN_CRITIQUE:87) but heldout_hashes.json is frozen at question_count=58 (frozen_at 2026-07-13T07:55:14Z) while all three captured EVAL_2026-07-13_*.json baselines have n=56. Two questions were added after baseline capture; any A/B against 'the 56' must subset by id or re-baseline.
- **[eval] contamination firewall**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'contamination' means two unrelated things. Here = eval-set leakage into production representations. In P0.5 it = facet metadata pollution ('corpus-lens facet contamination', CHECKLIST:118; backend/scripts/p0_5_facet_decontamination.py). Do not route P0.5 facet work through eval_firewall or vice versa. Also note: is_heldout_query has ZERO production call sites today — its only importer is freeze_heldout_eval.py:29; the checklist's automated eval-run contamination check (CHECKLIST:584-587) is deferred to P2.2 and is PLAN-ONLY.
- **[eval] eval**: FAILURE MODE (b): the plan's single word 'eval' is three disjoint code harnesses that do not share scoring code. run_heldout_eval.score() re-implements recall/hit inline and never imports eval_metrics (eval_metrics' only consumer is three_tier_eval.py:14). Concretely: P1.1 box CHECKLIST:570-571 is checked [x] claiming 'nDCG/MRR' were captured, but the heldout runner computes no nDCG/MRR and EVAL_*.json summaries contain no such keys — nDCG/MRR exist only in the un-wired eval_metrics.py. The checked box overstates what the deployed scorer measures.
- **[eval] baseline**: FAILURE MODE (a): one word, three artifact species. In P1.1/S8 ('A/B on the held-out 56 vs the 2026-07-13 baseline', PLAN_CRITIQUE:87) 'baseline' = EVAL_*.json quality scores. In the Implementation Log ('Baseline capture (pre-edit requirement)', CHECKLIST:1272) 'baseline' = the census BASELINE_*.json + LATENCY_*.json. P1.2's acceptance 'improves materially over baseline' (CHECKLIST:611) means the EVAL numbers. A reader who fetches the wrong species will compare counts against recall rates.
- **[eval] regression matrix**: FAILURE MODE (b), high risk: matrix rows 1-12 (CHECKLIST:1224-1235: expert direct hit, naive bridge, single fact, broad, list, procedural, comparison, follow-up, negative control, cross-domain, cross-corpus, cross-corpus-irrelevant) are the heldout suite's shape taxonomy under different names (heldout shapes: direct, naive, single_fact, broad, list, procedural, comparison, followup, negative_control, cross_domain, cross_corpus, cross_corpus_irrelevant — freeze_heldout_eval.py:31-44). Only rows 13-16 (no-tree corpus, deleted corpus, cold-start, concurrent-ingest) are new. Building the matrix as a third standalone harness would triplicate scoring; the honest build is heldout shapes + 4 ops rows + evaluate_route_result's record contract. Also (a): 'regression suite' elsewhere means the ordinary pytest suite (docs/QUERY_PLAN_V2_RETRIEVAL.md:221) — not this matrix.
- **[eval] doc_hit**: FAILURE MODE (b): one idea implemented twice — run_heldout_eval.doc_hit and eval_metrics.exact_source_hit_at_k compute the same binary hit independently, and their semantics already diverge: doc_hit flips to ALL-expected-docs-required when the question sets expected_all_docs (run_heldout_eval.py:188-191); exact_source_hit_at_k is fixed any-hit@k with a k cutoff the heldout runner doesn't apply. Any consolidation must preserve the expected_all_docs branch or list/comparison questions will silently score easier.
- **[eval] negative controls**: FAILURE MODE (a): one phrase, two different assertions — (i) 'an unanswerable question must be refused' (heldout shape + REFUSAL_RE + probe_tier_latency) and (ii) 'this vocabulary term must never be introduced by expansion' (three_tier_eval forbidden lexicon). Also mild (b): the unanswerable-question control exists three times (heldout suite, latency probe, strict-ready smoke requirement CHECKLIST:1268) with no shared question source — the tungsten query is hardcoded in the probe, not drawn from the suite's 5 negative_control rows.
- **[eval] before/after**: FAILURE MODE (a): CHECKLIST:1246 'Candidate counts before/after fusion' uses the identical words for per-run pipeline-stage counts inside one query — unrelated to change gating. FAILURE MODE (b): 'before/after evals' (shelf_reserve), 'A/B gate + golden battery' (waterfall), and P1.1's acceptance gate (CHECKLIST:591-592, unchecked) all describe the same missing comparison harness under three names — real risk each feature grows its own one-off A/B script.
- **[eval] preregistered thresholds**: FAILURE MODE (a) adjacent: 'threshold' in code overwhelmingly means runtime production gates (ANSWERABILITY_COVERAGE_THRESHOLD, backend/services/answerability_tuning.py:97) — tuning knobs, not eval pass/fail bars; do not preregister by reusing those settings. The substantive gap: the checklist's eval acceptance criteria are qualitative ('improves materially over baseline' CHECKLIST:611, 'no held-out recall/nDCG loss' CHECKLIST:831) with no stored numbers, so today nothing is preregistered — the only pre-declared numerics anywhere are the latency budgets and the (unset) per-case min_* floors.
- **[eval] scorer**: FAILURE MODE (a): 'scorer' elsewhere in the codebase means production RANKING scorers — services/retriever/lexical.py:49 (fallback lexical scorer), services/retriever/evidence_allocation.py:13,66 (metadata-aware scorer), services/graph/orchestrator.py:2715 (graph ranking-signal scorer). Same word, retrieval-time concept, never an eval concept. FAILURE MODE (b): three parallel eval scorers (score(), evaluate_route_result, evaluate_case) with no shared code. Hygiene bug: the in-file comment still says 'scorer v2' (run_heldout_eval.py:45) while HEAD is v3 (commit e1d4a4f) and artifacts stamp scorer_version=3 — the comment is the kind of stale tag PLAN_CRITIQUE C4 warns about.
- **[leftover] ledger**: None — 'ledger' and 'implementation ledger' are one artifact; the checklist self-declares it.
- **[leftover] execution plan**: The ledger is item truth, the plan file is its ORDERING (checklist:8-12) — two docs, one plan-of-record; do not treat them as independent plans.
- **[leftover] s0-s14**: Step ids exist only in the plan doc; session Tasks #18/#19 mirror S1/S3 by name — keep ids in sync when the plan is re-sequenced.
- **[leftover] plan critique**: COLLISION (a): 'critique' also names a DIFFERENT 2026-07-12 artifact set — docs/RAPTOR_RAG_CRITIQUE_AND_ROADMAP.md + RAPTOR_CRITIQUE_RESPONSE_2026-07-12.md + RAPTOR_CRITIQUE_ACKNOWLEDGEMENT_2026-07-12.md (external review + maintainer response). The 2026-07-13 plan critique is a separate sequencing audit. Cite the date.
- **[leftover] baseline commit**: COLLISION (a): 'baseline' means three things — (1) this git ref (checklist:4), (2) the durable-data baseline captured by backend/scripts/capture_raptor_baseline.py into docs/baselines/BASELINE_2026-07-13.json ('Current Durable Baseline' section, checklist:75-95), (3) the held-out eval baseline (docs/baselines/EVAL_2026-07-13_*.json, S8 A/B 'vs the 2026-07-13 baseline'). Always qualify which baseline.
- **[leftover] capture-before-rebuild**: No code enforcement exists — the rule is prose in the ledger + repo CLAUDE.md north-star. Nearest seam for a guard: the rebuild entry points backend/scripts/build_librarian_cards.py, backend/scripts/backfill_corpus_lexicon.py, backend/services/ingestion/summary_backfill.py.
- **[leftover] capture hook**: T-HOOK-3 (docling publication-vs-file-date de-conflation, S2) has NO code counterpart yet — to-be-built; nearest seam backend/services/ingestion/docling_adapter.py. Fields existing in the contract is NOT data coverage: plan-verified 0 rows carry temporal_class.
- **[leftover] owner waiver**: Pure process; no code or store records a waiver. If waivers matter, the ledger is the only ledger of them.
- **[leftover] dark fields**: 'Dark fields' (captured field without consumer) vs 'dark code' (merged code not deployed, S0/C3) are sibling but distinct hygiene failures — the plan uses both; don't collapse them.
- **[leftover] status tag**: 'IN CODE' is used in the critique table but is NOT defined in the Status Legend (checklist:38-44) — undefined tag in the vocabulary; worth adding to the legend.
- **[leftover] stale**: COLLISION (a): ledger-'stale' (a status tag contradicted by a green verify, e.g. P0.1's two IN PROGRESS tags) vs code-'stale' (cache/epoch staleness, provider_canary_cache). Same word, unrelated mechanisms.
- **[leftover] migration**: COLLISION (a): one word covers (1) the Status Legend tag, (2) the executed backfill scripts, (3) the pending Neo4j edge migration (S12) and Qdrant collection consolidation (P3.3). Standing rule 4 'one migration per seam' governs (3). In code the executed form is almost always called 'backfill', not 'migration' — name drift.
- **[leftover] seam**: Not a code symbol; each named seam resolves to a concrete contract module. Keep the plan's seam→file mapping explicit or 'one migration per seam' is unenforceable.
- **[leftover] read-before-act**: No enforcement hook exists; the rule lives in checklist:28-30 and CLAUDE.md north-star. Nearest seam if automated: a Claude Code hook that re-opens the checklist at phase start.
- **[leftover] session memory**: Do not confuse with mem0/agent memory systems elsewhere in the user's stack — here it strictly means an agent acting on its recollection of the ledger instead of the file on disk (the C1/C2 root cause).
- **[leftover] acceptance tests**: Ledger 'acceptance' includes durable-data probes and live probes, not just pytest; many acceptance lines have no automated counterpart yet (e.g. the 16x3 regression matrix, checklist:52) — those are to-be-built, nearest seam three_tier_eval/run_heldout_eval.
- **[leftover] partial**: COLLISION (a): 'partial' also appears as partial-stage retry (checklist:502, P0.6 job semantics) and as the planned temporal capability level 'temporal_partial' (S6). Tag vs mechanism vs capability level.
- **[leftover] experiment**: No experiment framework exists in code; the before/after harness is run_heldout_eval.py + docs/baselines artifacts — nearest seam for P3.4/P3.5 experiments.
- **[leftover] retrieval tiers**: COLLISION (a): 'tier' also names Tier-0 doc-summary routing (config.py TIER0_ROUTING — a routing stage, not a RetrievalTier) and SourceChunk.source_tier (per-chunk provenance). See registry_retrieval.json 'tier' row.
- **[leftover] fast**: 'Fast' is a human label that exists only in docs/probe names; code always says qdrant_only. Note test_planned_retrieval.py:225 'planned fast' = QueryPlanV2 over qdrant_only — same tier, planned route.
- **[leftover] hybrid**: COLLISION (a): 'hybrid' ALSO means dense+sparse hybrid vector search inside Qdrant (qdrant_writer.py:958 'named=... sparse=...') — a scoring mechanism orthogonal to the store tier. A 'hybrid' result can come from any tier.
- **[leftover] graph**: COLLISION (a), strong: 'graph' = (1) the tier, (2) the Neo4j subsystem, (3) the _graph Qdrant collection kind, (4) Graph View frontend. Plan text usually means (1); code greps for 'graph' hit all four.
- **[leftover] corpus boundary**: No single 'boundary' symbol; the invariant is enforced at three layers (filter threading, per-corpus collections, graph properties). A test asserting the invariant end-to-end does not exist as one artifact — checklist:50 remains open.
- **[leftover] top-down retrieval**: The invariant (checklist:51-52) is broader than any one flag: TIER0_ROUTING covers doc routing; shelf routing (P1.4) and tree descent (Phase 2) are separate unbuilt/partial pieces of the same invariant. Duplicate-implementation risk (b): Tier-0 routing and P1.4 shelf routing both answer 'which documents first' — S-plan must wire shelf routing THROUGH Tier-0, not beside it.
- **[leftover] semantic drift**: No symbol named 'drift'; the invariant (checklist:54-55) is realized by lane protection plus S5's 'gated query-expansion consumption (original-query lane protected)'. Same concept as the 'original query' row.
- **[leftover] final evidence**: No `final_evidence` symbol; three modules co-own finalization (ranking_policy, reservation_policy, final_selector). Checklist:479 'no separator/navigation artifact can enter a final evidence packet' is still open — nearest seam is the NOISY_KINDS junk filter.
- **[leftover] corpus_id**: Note Neo4j uses the PLURAL corpus_ids[] (shared entities across corpora) — same identity, different cardinality by store.
- **[leftover] schema version**: One field name, many independent version namespaces — that is by design; the invariant (checklist:58-59) requires it on every generated artifact family.
- **[leftover] abstractive summary**: Defined negatively in code: abstractive = NOT an extractive-fallback and NOT an empty-model placeholder. The positive marker is the summary_model provenance field.
- **[leftover] extractive fallback**: DUPLICATE-IMPLEMENTATION (b): the same idea is implemented twice under near-identical names — ghost_a._extractive_fallback_summary (parents) and summary_tree._extractive_fallback (tree nodes). Per-seam duplication is currently intentional, but checklist:955 ('never create extractive fallback placeholders after provider failure') must be enforced at BOTH sites; fixing one will not fix the other.
- **[leftover] hardcoded topic rules**: The term names an ANTI-pattern: code exists (query_semantics curated lists) and the plan's work is its removal/migration (checklist:62-63 invariant; P0.5 'curated aliases -> versioned lexicon'; S5 registry). Grepping for a 'topic_rules' symbol finds nothing — the rules hide inside query_semantics constants.
- **[leftover] fail closed**: TWO mirror gates share the knobs (services/answerability_tuning.py): keep retriever gate STRICT, tune chat gate — loosening the wrong one breaks either fail-closed or answer coverage.
- **[leftover] pressure gates**: Two modules (pressure.py = pipeline/provider, storage_pressure.py = Qdrant memory) — complementary, not duplicates; the invariant (checklist:65-66) requires BOTH active during backfills.
- **[leftover] durable leases**: COLLISION (a): one plan term, two implementations with different semantics and test surfaces. The P0.6 open 'lease test matrix' (restart-before-expiry, purge-beyond-lease) targets the CLEANUP lease only — a green lane-lease suite proves nothing about it.
- **[leftover] idempotent replay**: No single symbol; the invariant (checklist:65-66) is a property each job family implements separately (summary jobs, extraction jobs, graph promotion, lexicon slices). checklist:502 adds partial-stage retry to the same family.
- **[leftover] api keys**: Invariant (checklist:67-68) is about never printing/committing them; enforcement is convention + encryption at the settings boundary, no scanner exists in-repo.
- **[leftover] deterministic policy**: Spans two layers (retriever reservation + librarian roles) — see the 'document seats' collision row; the invariant text (checklist:69-73) covers both.
- **[leftover] document seats**: COLLISION (a) + duplicate-implementation risk (b): two seat systems at different granularity. S8 wires shelf_reserve THROUGH reservation_policy ('never the old unconditional floor') — building librarian seats as a second independent reservation path is the explicitly-banned duplicate.
- **[leftover] summary points**: Distinct from Tier-0 doc-summary vectors in polymath_doc_summaries (doc-level, config.py:645) — 'summary point' in the durable-baseline counts (checklist:77-84) means the parent-level points.
- **[leftover] polymath_v2**: 'v2' shorthand in the plan always means this corpus, not schema polymath.extract.v2 — beware when grepping.
- **[leftover] ecommerce_ai_film_school**: Name-case drift: harvested term is lowercase but the store name is mixed-case — case-sensitive Mongo queries with the lowercase form return nothing.
- **[leftover] ugo_corpus**: Same case-drift hazard as ecommerce_AI_FILM_SCHOOL.
- **[leftover] rollups**: Do not confuse with S5 'alias/latent rollup' (PLAN_CRITIQUE:84) — that is a DIFFERENT, to-be-built aggregation (parent latent_concepts -> doc profile -> lexicon), sharing only the word. Flag when reading S5.
- **[leftover] qdrant collections**: P3.3 'collection consolidation' plans to change this layout — a migration-tagged item; until then _col_for_corpus is the only legal resolver.
- **[leftover] latency probes**: The checklist's 'Recent deployed latency probes: Fast 39.8s degraded...' (line 91) are this script's outputs; P1.9 per-stage timing is a separate, unbuilt finer-grained instrument.
- **[leftover] reranker readiness**: The DEPLOYED reranker per user memory is the torch fp16 sidecar on :8081 (plist-managed) while reranker_mlx is the rollback backend — verify which binary serves :8081 before trusting readiness semantics. Repo also contains a /reranker docker service with NO warmup (grep empty) — third implementation of 'the reranker'.
- **[leftover] embedder /health**: DUPLICATE-IMPLEMENTATION (b): TWO embedder services exist — repo /embedder (docker, NO warmup code) and scripts/apple_ml_services/embedder_mlx (host MLX :8082, has P1.8 warmup). The deployed one is embedder_mlx (docker-compose.override routes EMBEDDER_URL to host :8082). Checklist line 93-95 ('Embedder /health ... does not certify a completed inference warmup') predates the merged warmup — now stale per checklist:746-761 receipts.

- **[leftover] claim audit**: No code; the auditable-claims machinery is capture_raptor_baseline.py + the verify subcommands (nearest seam), and session Task #17 'Exec-plan audit workflow: every checklist claim -> auditable action' is the unbuilt automation. Related but distinct docs: RAPTOR_CRITIQUE_RESPONSE_2026-07-12.md (maintainer response) and PLAN_CRITIQUE_2026-07-13.md (sequencing critique).

## Execution Flows — concept aggregation onto S-steps

*(Orchestrator-authored: the flows agent was a spend-limit casualty; flows below derive from the end-state map + registry.
Canonical names per the registry.)*

- **latent/underlying concepts** (canonical: `latent_concepts`; NOT latent_topics, NOT summary_tree.concepts):
  S1 contract seam carries them per-parent → S4 one paid pass fills the pair → S5 rollup EXTENDS `doc_profile.concepts`
  (which already exists — do not re-derive) + fixes the Qdrant payload whitelist that currently DROPS latent_concepts →
  S8 cards consume via the existing `candidate_latent_subjects` corroborate-only path → S10 P2.2 admission.
- **aliases** (canonical: ONE versioned registry absorbing the 3 existing stores — lexicon identity evidence,
  curated CONCEPT_ALIASES in Python, latent_concepts[].aliases): S4 captures → S5 builds the registry + query-time
  expansion through the EXISTING grounded gate (original-lane protection already in code) → S8 card fields.
  MUST also reconcile the TWO entity_id builders (lexicon `_entity_id` vs graph `entity_id_from_name`) in S5.
- **facets**: S7 DF-admission rule (owner decision) + cleanup riding S5's payload rewrite; unify the duplicate
  alias tables (`_CONTENT_FACET_ALIASES` vs `_CHAT_COVERAGE_FACETS`) and the two broad-alias gates in the same pass;
  note `agency_preservation` is still stampable on NEW ingests — S7 includes the ingest-side gate, not just cleanup.
- **temporal**: S1 (summary temporal_class/time_expressions — the SUMMARY seam, distinct from the chunk-level
  `temporal_captures` already live) → S2 bibliographic/date de-conflation (settle `source_published_at` as the
  canonical name; `published_at` in P2.1 is the same concept) → S4 pair backfill → S6 temporal readiness → S12 T-MAIN.
- **hierarchy/headers** (`heading_path` == `section_path`, one field): S3 disposition matrix (SIGNED?) →
  projection heading-repair (free) → prov-capture code change if page_start is wanted (reingest alone can NEVER add it)
  → S4 rides reingested subset if approved.
- **extraction**: P2.4 negation → P2.5 typed signatures → P2.6 parity → S11 ONE paid burst (pair only, v2 frozen)
  with T-HOOK-1 temporal aboard → P2.8 grounding. External parallel-session work on semantic contracts/spaCy
  (branch `claude-continuation-20260713`) slots HERE and must merge before S11 runs.
- **librarian/seats**: S0 merged shelf_reserve DARK → S8 flips only via before/after A/B on the frozen held-out set;
  disambiguate `shelf` (P1.4 corpus-routing sense is PLAN-ONLY; P1.5 role sense is in code);
  `reserve_corpora` still runs and is NOT superseded — S8 must reconcile it with `reservation_policy` explicitly.
- **readiness**: S6 three-way split (operational / metadata-quality / temporal) consuming S2+S4 fields; strict-ready
  gates (GTE chunk) close at S14.
- **eval spine**: frozen 58q + firewall gates EVERY flip: S8 (shelf), S10 (P2.2 pilot), S11 (parity), S14 (16×3 matrix).

### Cross-flow dependencies
S1 → S4 (capture before paid pass); S2 → S8 (bibliographic before cards); S3 → S4 subset & S11 (disposition before spend);
S4 → S5 (capture before rollup); S5 → S7 cleanup rides its rewrite; S5+S2 → S8 (cards last); S8 → S9/S10 (consumption
after measurement); P2.4–2.6 (+ external contracts branch) → S11; S6 → S12; everything → S14.

## Audit Ledger — every claim, every disposition

### Header / Standing Rules / Legend / Invariants / Baseline (frozen lines 1-96, chunk HDR)
